< text>
Idan is the greatest locksmith we have ever encountered.

We moved into a house that has a 50 year old Baldwin Mortise lock on the front door.  It wasn't working correctly and we had taken it apart ourselves, which was a big mistake because we could not get all the pieces back together! ... As a result, the lock box no longer worked correctly and they are very expensive to replace new.

Long story short, we found Idan on Yelp and he was able to repair the mortise lock in less than an hour.

While performing the repair, he was also able to make other adjustments to the springs and to the key barrel, and the lock is now working perfectly.  Idan explained every step he took to repair the lock and encouraged repairing mortise locks over simply replacing with new ones.

Overall, he provides top notch customer service and has a vast knowledge of how mortise locks operate.  We highly recommend him for any locksmith services.<//text>

< username>
Doug M.<//username>
<Text>First time eater as I went in with a co-worker who had been here before. I ordered an Ortega burger and fries. This is not a fast food place and your order will take a few minutes for it to cook, but it is worth the short wait. Both Burger and fries were very good. It's hard to find crinkle french fries anywhere these days, but this place had them and I enjoyed them. As for the hamburger it was worthy of a billboard picture. And that's the good news.

The bad news is this was an expensive lunch. For the aforementioned items plus an iced tea the bill ran me $15 plus. That's almost exactly what Five Guys had charged me for basically the same thing. As good as my lunch was, I think it could have been a little bit cheaper. And I would be remissed not to point out that the inside dining area was filled with smoke from the kitchen and it was actually difficult to breathe in there. Fortunately it was a nice day and we were able to eat outside.

Overall I'd say this place is not a bad choice for a good lunch, but due to its prices I recommend you do it infrequently.

Edited on 4/10/19 because I was rushed and didn't proofread my previous posting. Hopefully that first paragraph wasn't too off-putting.</Text>< Gmap_id>

I've been a Rubio's fan since Ralph Rubio opened in San Diego.  Unfortunately he extended his reach to Ventura and things fell apart.  When they've got someone in the kitchen who cares they are wonderful.  But today sadly they were not.
The prepare each dish to order and are not fast.  So relax and sit outside on the patio and listen to the speaker blare out instructions in English and Spanish on a 20 second loop  to wait outside.  That's coming from their Chinese neighbor.
The staff is the typical unmanaged sort that doesn't like their job and takes it out on customers.  No need lady to slam the soda bottle down on the counter so it fizzes all over me when I open it.  And no need to throw the salsa menu at me either.

< review>
We really enjoyed this spot. We decided to skip our regular spot and try this one. It was a great decision. The atmosphere was fun with great music. They have a bar area and a regular sitting area which has individual TV service in each booth(great for football season).

There was no line, so we waited about 7 minutes. The host was friendly and welcoming. Our waitress was awesome and ready to provide great service. And she did that!

A full bar is such a plus. Didn't care for my drink too much, but my husband selected it so I'll just blame him..lol.

The food. Seasoning was on point. We ordered the sampler deal, extra side of 1lb of shrimp, calamari and wings. The seafood with the cajun mixed seasoning delicious. Calamari I loved it,  but my daughter liked the other spot better,  the wings were cooked to hard. The seasoning on them were good, but I don't like to fight with my food. Also the spice level was ok. There spicy is not spicy. I guess when I do stop in again I'll try the omg spice level. Maybe that will be the level of hot we like.

Overall we do like the spot and will come back. Still stuck on our original spot since we have been there since opening, but it's good to know i have another option close by.< /review>

<userid>107434908954743368047<//userid>< username>
Stocks Huskies (Stocks and Huskies)</username>
< date>
1493659693682<//date>
<Rating>2< /Rating><Text>The Crabby Crab could be decent, yet the service is absolutely horrendous at times.  In my reviews this usually offsets almost any of the food's taste, as I could make the food myself and bypass the bad service.

When we first walked in, we noticed that the young service girl at the door does not know whether she is supposed to be helping the kitchen or the big party tables (to try to cash in on tips).  She is not a waitress, so I am not sure where the discrepancy came in;  she didn't help out with any other tables and the guys from the back deliver food and clean up the table at the end sooooo... that brings us to case #2.

Our starting waiter did not look like he wanted to be there that day.  We had our appetizers before our drinks because he forgot them ... a negative mark in the restaurant industry.  He even dropped off our check at the end (after we started being served by another waiter) and told us he had to go move his car ... before not coming back to get the check.  Even on our way out, the original waiter was hiding in the kitchen instead of getting our tab.  I tipped the other waiter with glasses who was absolutely great, who noticed the bad service towards the end and stepped up.  I wish I could tip the guy who brought our food out too;  he was very punctual with bringing our order and always had a smile on his face.

As stated above, we ordered two mixed drinks.  Standard watered down drinks that I do not remember: one had blue curacao and the other coconut.  They did not warrant a second round.

The fried oysters were fried somewhat hard and had a cheap sweet and sour sauce paired with them ... truthfully, this should come with a remoulade or tartar sauce.

The crab cakes were fried to a nice consistency and the insides were moist.  Good job here and the salad on the side gives you something to eat with it;  yet, again, a tartar sauce or Thousand Island-based sauce would be a nice pairing - as squeezing lemon only takes it so far.

They were out of the snow crab and lobster when we got there, so we had to deal with king crab - since dungeness takes too much work for me and they charge $30/pound for something I will mostly throw away.  King crab tastes just like snow crab after seasoning, in my opinion;  however, trying to get into king crab is a whole different beast.  I dealt with it, but not what I expected to do that day;  it reduced the amount of pounds I ordered to one since I can't stand the spikiness.  And let's be honest, $35 a pound is a limiting factor too.

The shrimp were cooked nicely but the Crabby Way flavor did not impart to the meat well - as they were headed (with two or three being mushy towards the head part of the bodies).  I would suggest having the heads taken off, but that is my preference.

Since I base most of my reviews off of service, you can just go to the place and hope that your experience is different.  Service is atrocious at times,  they were out of the things they sell the most of (which is also a negative in the restaurant industry for something you 'specialize' in), prices are too high for the location (Van Nuys is LA ... but not upscale LA), and the food that you're getting is par for the course for what I expect a decent crab place should serve (not mind-blowingly good, but cooked well).

The waiter with glasses pretty much is the one you want.  If he had been our waiter from the beginning (and possibly worked the door), this rating may have been higher.  Make sure to ask for him and tip him, if you go.< /Text><pics>None< /pics><Response>None< /Response>< gmapID>
